  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dd682d4c-238c-43e9-961a-592eadbf3327'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText1422365429727681030" style="display:none">Still avoiding magic whenever possible, Corporal Kaylin Neya relished investigating a regular theft once again. Until she found out the mysterious box was taken from Elani Street, where the mages and charlatans mingled, and it was sometimes hard to tell the difference between the two. But she was hoping this might be a mundane case-- --when in a back room Kaylin saw a lost-looking girl in a reflective pool...who called out Kaylin's name.<br /><br />Shaken, Kaylin tried to stay focused on the case at hand. But since the stolen item was ancient, without a keyhole, and held tremendous darkness inside, Kaylin knew unknown forces were again playing with her destiny--and her life....</span>

<div id="review_1713418741" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1713418741" />
    <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans"><img alt="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587115780p2/7298986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1713418741?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans">✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21128306-cast-in-secret">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=humongous-potential-goes-poof">humongous-potential-goes-poof</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=cure-for-insomnia">cure-for-insomnia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=boredom-fest">boredom-fest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=welcome-to-the-zoo">welcome-to-the-zoo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=tbr-shelf-says-thank-you">tbr-shelf-says-thank-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=blah-blah-blah-heaven">blah-blah-blah-heaven</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713418741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5942046985591129308"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465975513i/19422225._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b><u>Actual rating</u>: 2.5 stars</b>. <br/><br/>I've said it before, and I'll say it again: this is one of the <b>richest, most interesting, original Fantasy worlds</b> I've ever come across. And yet…<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471274495ra/20019042.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Yep, that's right</b>. Because there is only so much <b>boredom</b> I can take. And <b>Bloody Fantastic Elantra</b> (BFE™) or not, I've had it. I've had it with the incessant, irrelevant <b>blah-blah-blah-ing</b>. And with the non-stop, unnecessary, uninteresting <b>info dumping</b>. And with the painfully <b>slow pace</b>. And with the <b>ever-jumbled plot</b> that makes</span>
  <span id="freeText5942046985591129308" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465975513i/19422225._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b><u>Actual rating</u>: 2.5 stars</b>. <br><br>I've said it before, and I'll say it again: this is one of the <b>richest, most interesting, original Fantasy worlds</b> I've ever come across. And yet…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471274495ra/20019042.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Yep, that's right</b>. Because there is only so much <b>boredom</b> I can take. And <b>Bloody Fantastic Elantra</b> (BFE™) or not, I've had it. I've had it with the incessant, irrelevant <b>blah-blah-blah-ing</b>. And with the non-stop, unnecessary, uninteresting <b>info dumping</b>. And with the painfully <b>slow pace</b>. And with the <b>ever-jumbled plot</b> that makes me feel like a <b>harebrained nitwit</b>. And with the total and utter lack of <b>character development</b>. Kaylin, my dear, you could have made it into my Cool Chicks Harem, but you keep <b>blabbering like an immature teenager</b> just like you did in the first instalment, and I've had enough. I have been <b>anxiously waiting</b> to know more about you and the mysteriously mysterious symbols on your body since book one, but you know what? I have no patience left. <b>And I don't give a bloody damn anymore</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471275496i/20019128.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Come to think of it</b>, this whole world and the characters in it seem to have <b>stopped their progression/evolution</b> at the end of book 1. Nothing new or exciting has happened since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9542.Cast_in_Shadow__Chronicles_of_Elantra___1_" title="Cast in Shadow (Chronicles of Elantra, #1) by Michelle Sagara" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Shadow</a>, and it feels like the author <b>hit the freeze button</b> on her writing remote ← <i>don't ask me what a writing remote is supposed to be, I have no freaking idea.</i> I usually love it when authors take their time to develop the world they created (not <u>too</u> much time though, I am, after all, little <s>slightly</s> impatient me), but this is overdoing it. <b>We are stuck, my Little Barnacles</b>! Irremediably and hopelessly stuck! I probably would have enjoyed this one a lot more had the story been <s>half</s> as interesting as it was in book 1. <b>But it wasn't, so I didn't</b>. Enjoy it, I mean. Besides, the plot in this one is about a missing kid. And you know just how much I love <b>Kids and Babes and Infants Oh My</b> (KaBaIOM™), don't you, my Lovely Decapods? So I guess what I'm ever-so-cleverly trying to say is: it would take a <b>seriously awesome story</b> to make me care about a <s>freaking</s> missing kid. This one happened to be <b>seriously NOT awesome</b>, so I didn't. Care, I mean. <br> <br>» <b>And the moral of this Crappy Non Review is: I. AM. DONE.</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471277299i/20019317._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>· <b>Book 0.5</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1286085853" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Moonlight</a> ★★★★<br>· <b>Book 1</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109559774" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Shadow</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 2</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1287696138" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Courtlight</a> ★★★★ (make that 3.5 stars. Because I was in a good mood when I wrote the Crappy Non Review.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5942046985591129308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText14078921516356167868" style="display:none">Welp, Kaylin is still a stumbling, bumbling idiot who refuses to learn jack and somehow is still alive, despite her nonstop nonsense talking. She doesn't annoy me enough to hate these books, but she definitely brings them down. <br /><br />This time around is about the Thal'anni, the mind reader people with tentacles on their head. One of their kids goes missing and Kaylin has to find the child. Right up her usual alley. <br /><br />Highlights: more dragons, Severn, Evanton, the Oracles, Everly, and all the very interesting elementals. <br /><br />I think this book seemed shorter than the others, which is good because I'm not super interested in the tentacle people. Severn is still hot and I'm still wondering why he likes Kaylin. Nightshade is still in the picture, in the weird crush triangle going on. I'd say love triangle, but there's no romance, it's kind of like "I could maybe have a crush on you." I like Nightshade, he's all odd and mysterious + you know he's only talking to Kaylin for his own angles. <br /><br />The ending was interesting, could've been more bloody and murderous; I'm underwhelmed on that part. Fingers crossed the next book gets more stabby. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1214626593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer518426929366228799">These books read like police procedurals with a smart-mouthed officer with a blinding weakness for children, but in a world overflowing with mysterious magic and cool species. So not really action-oriented, but gripping if you enjoy investigations that involve talking to witnesses and putting the pieces together. All of that builds to the end, when I find myself reading so fast I forget to blink. All without swords! (However, there are knives.)<br/><br/>The investigations are centered on crimes, but the m</span>
  <span id="freeText518426929366228799" style="display:none">These books read like police procedurals with a smart-mouthed officer with a blinding weakness for children, but in a world overflowing with mysterious magic and cool species. So not really action-oriented, but gripping if you enjoy investigations that involve talking to witnesses and putting the pieces together. All of that builds to the end, when I find myself reading so fast I forget to blink. All without swords! (However, there are knives.)<br /><br />The investigations are centered on crimes, but the more fascinating mysteries are the magic and world with its multiple species, and these really take center stage. Each book so far has illuminated a new aspect of the world and magic, becoming more intriguing as the picture clears. I don't always understand everything at first, but I get a general idea and carry on, and it becomes more clear as it goes. I love that it feels like there's so much left to learn in future books, too.<br /><br />This book in particular illuminates the Tha'alani, one of the mortal races. I really enjoyed them much more than I expected! <br /><br />Kaylin is still impulsive and driven mostly by instinct when it comes to magic, but she's learning. She's also learning to keep her mouth shut occasionally. To say anymore than that would be to spoil it, so I won't. Enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="518426929366228799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9414824364123862879">I don't know exactly what it is about these books, but I really find them enjoyable to read. The fantasy world created by Sagara is incredibly rich and original, and I like the way she adds to the world with each installment. I also appreciate how each book works as a complete story by itself, but also adds pieces to the larger story arc that is developing in the series.<br/><br/>This time we got to learn a lot more about the Tha'alani, a mortal race of telepaths that Kaylin has previously been fearful of</span>
  <span id="freeText9414824364123862879" style="display:none">I don't know exactly what it is about these books, but I really find them enjoyable to read. The fantasy world created by Sagara is incredibly rich and original, and I like the way she adds to the world with each installment. I also appreciate how each book works as a complete story by itself, but also adds pieces to the larger story arc that is developing in the series.<br /><br />This time we got to learn a lot more about the Tha'alani, a mortal race of telepaths that Kaylin has previously been fearful of. It was interesting to see Kaylin face her racial prejudice, and her process of trying to understand and overcome it. I would have liked a bit more of Severn, who continues to be a great character, but there are so many interesting characters that I was happy to spend time with others as well. Once again the parts where magic is used were very well written, and there was a nice balance between mystery and action.<br /><br />I'm so curious to see where the story goes next in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3309615.Cast_in_Fury__Chronicles_of_Elantra__4_" title="Cast in Fury (Chronicles of Elantra #4) by Michelle Sagara" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Fury</a>.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_140318000" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140318000" />
    <a title="Ithlilian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4793655-ithlilian"><img alt="Ithlilian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392859819p2/4793655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140318000?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ithlilian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ithlilian" href="/user/show/4793655-ithlilian">Ithlilian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4793655-ithlilian?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140318000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5012277075783257055">I enjoyed the first book in this series because it was different, compelling, and interesting. I enjoyed the second one because it was similar, but some of the things that bothered me about the first book started to get to me in the second book. Now, the things that annoyed me in previous books are all that I see, and I'm about finished giving this series a chance. The worst thing about Cast in Secret is that it doesn't give any reason to continue the series. In the other books there were secret</span>
  <span id="freeText5012277075783257055" style="display:none">I enjoyed the first book in this series because it was different, compelling, and interesting. I enjoyed the second one because it was similar, but some of the things that bothered me about the first book started to get to me in the second book. Now, the things that annoyed me in previous books are all that I see, and I'm about finished giving this series a chance. The worst thing about Cast in Secret is that it doesn't give any reason to continue the series. In the other books there were secrets waiting to be uncovered and characters that were compelling, this book is just a long drawn out mystery. All of the things that have been wrong with the series since the beginning are still present. First, the characters. Kaylin is immature and has not progressed one bit. I would say she is dim witted, but I can't follow the events that are occurring any better than she can. Everyone knows more than the main character and they are not willing to share their information with her. It's extremely frustrating. The secondary characters don't appeal because no new information was gained about them in this book. I'd love to know more about Lord Nightshade but he's not sharing. As for the oracles and people with moth feelers on their heads, I couldn't care less. I've come to the point where the world is no longer new and exciting, the mysteries are convoluted and painful to follow, and the characters aren't as interesting as they once were. I'd love to know more about the symbols Kaylin has on her body, and about Nightshade. It doesn't seem like that will happen anytime soon, but I may continue just for that. Another problem I have is the writing style. The dialogue consists a of very short sentence from one character, followed by a one word reply from another character. For example:<br /><br />"Water," he said. "Tell me what you think."<br />She knew she was chewing on her lower lip. "Well," she said at last, "you can drown in it."<br />"Yes."<br />"And the storms at sea-"<br />"Yes."<br />"But if you don't drink it, you die."<br />"Very good."<br /><br />Or this:<br /><br />"If he's involved in this-"<br />"Yes."<br />"He never stopped."<br />"No."<br />"Severn?"<br />"Yes?"<br />"Did the Wolves hunt him?"<br />He didn't answer...<br /><br />I'm starting to think this book was written with no real purpose. The other books hinted at things to come, this one stayed in the present and gave us very little new information. I like when authors plan out their series instead of just throwing a book together around a mystery and some elementals. I would like to think this series is going somewhere instead of just stagnating. I would like to think something important will happen instead of just throwing Kaylin into quests she isn't intelligent enough to handle intelligently. Who knows what the next book would bring. I know that I'm sick of the writing style, the characters, the plot, the mystery, and everyone knowing things they never share. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5012277075783257055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2835154649585003176">**** 3.75 ****<br/><br/>I really like this series, the world building and the legend and mythology it creates! I would have given if a higher rating, but this particular case was quite slow to start, dragged in the middle, and the end was somewhat anticlimactic... I think I didn't get enough of the lion people and Kaylin acted like a bratty child most of the time. All of the supporting characters are telling her what I want to scream at her - IGNORANCE IS NOT COOL! Nor is it helpful... So, the author is a</span>
  <span id="freeText2835154649585003176" style="display:none">**** 3.75 ****<br /><br />I really like this series, the world building and the legend and mythology it creates! I would have given if a higher rating, but this particular case was quite slow to start, dragged in the middle, and the end was somewhat anticlimactic... I think I didn't get enough of the lion people and Kaylin acted like a bratty child most of the time. All of the supporting characters are telling her what I want to scream at her - IGNORANCE IS NOT COOL! Nor is it helpful... So, the author is aware of this and I am hoping she is going to grow little with every book, so I am going to be patient and wait, because the books are very compelling and have great potential!!!</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776234792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17518531961745003704">It seems that there's a pattern to these book. With each new instalment we get to know one of the races better. I wonder what will happen once we're out of races.<br/><br/>I really liked the Thaalani. I also understand why Kaylin and most of the other people in the Empire fear them. I value my privacy way too much appreciated someone who can randomly get in my head. At the same time I'm pretty sure that had I had a similar power I would turn hermit. Just seeing the utter stupidity people do and put on the</span>
  <span id="freeText17518531961745003704" style="display:none">It seems that there's a pattern to these book. With each new instalment we get to know one of the races better. I wonder what will happen once we're out of races.<br /><br />I really liked the Thaalani. I also understand why Kaylin and most of the other people in the Empire fear them. I value my privacy way too much appreciated someone who can randomly get in my head. At the same time I'm pretty sure that had I had a similar power I would turn hermit. Just seeing the utter stupidity people do and put on the internet makes me doubt that humanity should exists. <br /><br />The history of the Thaalani and their connection to the elements was really fascinating. The seers and their hall, the way it was organized to take care of beings who are unable due to their gifts to take care of themselves, is another thing that I liked. Basically I liked everything except Kaylin.<br /><br />Kaylin's continued insistence on staying ignorant, especially in the face of constantly needing someone to educate her on things she would have known had she listened at least a little during her classes gets me riled up each time. I just want to crawl into the book and slap her and then drag her to a school and chain her to a desk until she learns at least the basics of the world she lives in. She's not only not in the fiefs anymore but she's also one of the major players and she isn't dumb enough not to realize it. She might be in a state of denial but deep down she knows it. Just like every other character in the series knows it. So Kaylin, please stop acting like a juvenile and grow the f@ck up! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17518531961745003704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_73360010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73360010" />
    <a title="Coffcat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/350874-coffcat"><img alt="Coffcat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1214451199p2/350874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73360010?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Coffcat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Coffcat" href="/user/show/350874-coffcat">Coffcat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/350874-coffcat?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73360010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4253032866775674263">There's a couple of things I'd like to say about this book: <br/><br/>1. I really liked the story and all of the supporting characters. I like how new characters are being introduced and how we get more interactions with ones we already know. I felt like we got a good ways into the meat of the story. I would really like to see what happens next.<br/><br/>2. Big plot hole-"omg everyone is going to die!" so lets just send 2 people to investigate it. umm...I think a few more people might have been a good idea. What, w</span>
  <span id="freeText4253032866775674263" style="display:none">There's a couple of things I'd like to say about this book: <br /><br />1. I really liked the story and all of the supporting characters. I like how new characters are being introduced and how we get more interactions with ones we already know. I felt like we got a good ways into the meat of the story. I would really like to see what happens next.<br /><br />2. Big plot hole-"omg everyone is going to die!" so lets just send 2 people to investigate it. umm...I think a few more people might have been a good idea. What, were the other investigators too busy down at the donut shop?<br /><br />3. To sum up about 100 conversations in the book: "This is really important, but I can't just spell it out for you. You'll have to concentrate your little pea brain and figure it out yourself." Why do we have to be subjected to this over and over?!? The way we obtain information is not important! Working hard to discover something only gives us appreciation for it. She doesn't need to appreciate it-she needs it to save the world, so stop posturing and tell her what she freaking needs to know before my head explodes!<br /><br />4. I hate how Kaylin seems to be stuck in stasis. All of these wild experiences happen and it doesn't seem to change her at all. And don't get me started on how she can't keep her mouth shut and has zero manners. <i>Really?</i> I think the author is confused, these are not good characteristic for someone to have. It shows that she is not only ignorant but crass too. She's supposed to be the hero. It aggravates me even more when everyone is so accepting of it. "oh that's just Kaylin, yuck-yuck!" I just want to yell at the book "smack her a good one and maybe she'll remember to think before she speaks next time-geez!" I mean really-how old is she? 8 years old? cause she acts like it.<br /><br />I think the whole genre "my lead character is a strong woman cause she can't keep her mouth shut and runs blindly into dangerous situations" is getting ever so freaking old. A strong woman <u>can</u> can be smart and careful. Just because she has a mouth she can't keep shut, doesn't make her a hero, it makes her irritating. And that's not a compliment.<br /><br />~I don't usually get so emotional in my reviews-but this series could be so good and it's being held back by stupid mistakes. It makes me crazy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4253032866775674263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2666351084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2666351084" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6074441-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352692366p2/6074441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2666351084?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/6074441-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6074441-beth?shelf=fantasy-by-women">fantasy-by-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6074441-beth?shelf=2000s-sff-by-women">2000s-sff-by-women</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2666351084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer44420040321969142">As of its third volume, the Chronicles of Elantra has fallen into a sort of groove for me. The beginning is always interesting, the end is great, and the middle is very much a mixed bag. <br/><br/><i>Cast in Secret</i> largely deals with the telepathic Th'alani and the element of water <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[and their deep-rooted connection with each other <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I love the worldbuilding and descriptions in these books, especially when magic comes into play. The elemental grove behind Evanton's shop is a fasci</span>
  <span id="freeText44420040321969142" style="display:none">As of its third volume, the Chronicles of Elantra has fallen into a sort of groove for me. The beginning is always interesting, the end is great, and the middle is very much a mixed bag. <br /><br /><i>Cast in Secret</i> largely deals with the telepathic Th'alani and the element of water <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and their deep-rooted connection with each other <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I love the worldbuilding and descriptions in these books, especially when magic comes into play. The elemental grove behind Evanton's shop is a fascinating place, and the "basement" of Nightshade's castle was fun, too. New power is dangled in front of Kaylin, and because she is who she is, she tries to deny it rather than grabbing it with both hands, as most people would.<br /><br />I've become more accepting of Severn's role in these novels. He might act all Wolf-y and draw his weapon now and then, but what he's really there for is to be Kaylin's bulwark, to be her backup wherever she goes. The reader has to put up with a lot of "Severn said nothing" along the way. It'd be nice if he asserted himself beyond being a silent presence now and then.<br /><br />On the whole, these aren't action-packed books, though, and things have mellowed considerably since the first one, when characters--who are fairly docile now--literally threatened to kill one another almost as a matter of greeting. This one's almost on the cozy side, despite the epic-fantasy style world-threatening enemy <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who is dispatched offstage at the end of the book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />It was tempting to give this volume, and the previous one, better ratings because of their endings, both of which were moving and well-done. But I don't because of what I perceive as lackluster editing that lets so many repetitions of very tired phrases slip by. Don't create a drinking game around "He raised a brow" or somebody stomping on Kaylin's foot to get her to shut up....<br /><br />My attraction to this series, and my frustrations with it, continue. It has a unique vibe that I'll certainly be back to enjoy more of, and I'll try to be strong and not throw the next book against the wall when somebody raises their brow for the millionth damn time, or when the worldbuilding through dialogue goes on and on and on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="44420040321969142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40751426" />
    <a title="Latharia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/140880-latharia"><img alt="Latharia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1182310614p2/140880.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40751426?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Latharia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Latharia" href="/user/show/140880-latharia">Latharia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40751426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4391895728257461397">As with Cast In Courtlight, I really struggled to like this book. I read it primarily because I'd purchased it WITH Cast In Courtlight, after being so enthralled with the story of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9542.Cast_In_Shadow__Elantra_Book_1_' title='Cast In Shadow (Elantra Book 1) by Michelle Sagara West' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cast In Shadow</a>. Well, by Book #3 of the series, the heroine (Kaylin) hasn't developed an iota of common sense, which drives me absolutely batty. Supposedly in this book, the world's fate hangs on her ability to solve a mystery ... and everyone else seems to have crucial pieces of the puzzle, but they all persist in let</span>
  <span id="freeText4391895728257461397" style="display:none">As with Cast In Courtlight, I really struggled to like this book. I read it primarily because I'd purchased it WITH Cast In Courtlight, after being so enthralled with the story of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9542.Cast_In_Shadow__Elantra_Book_1_" title="Cast In Shadow (Elantra Book 1) by Michelle Sagara West" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast In Shadow</a>. Well, by Book #3 of the series, the heroine (Kaylin) hasn't developed an iota of common sense, which drives me absolutely batty. Supposedly in this book, the world's fate hangs on her ability to solve a mystery ... and everyone else seems to have crucial pieces of the puzzle, but they all persist in letting her find things out on her own, with these long-drawn-out "Ah, I wondered when you'd figure that out, Kaylin" speeches. When I can feel myself growing irritated and my brow furrowing in frustration that yet AGAIN, she can't seem to refrain from doing something idiotic, and AGAIN, others seem to feel it's crucial to enable her, and AGAIN, she learns not a damned thing about it ... it's time to move on to a different author!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4391895728257461397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_555945699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/555945699" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/555945699?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer555945699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7961689254857525622">Third in the Chronicles of Elantra fantasy series revolving around Kaylin, a young Hawk whom many fear should be killed.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>I don't get why the Quartermaster would even imagine that Kaylin would be able to get through a day without rips, tears, and bloodshed. He must know the situations she or any of the other Hawks go into…<br/><br/>Eew, eeeewww, spit, wipe, rub, just eewww. That is definitely an honor I could do without….ewwwwww….<br/><br/>It's a case in which Kaylin learns the truth about the Tha'alani. She a</span>
  <span id="freeText7961689254857525622" style="display:none">Third in the Chronicles of Elantra fantasy series revolving around Kaylin, a young Hawk whom many fear should be killed.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />I don't get why the Quartermaster would even imagine that Kaylin would be able to get through a day without rips, tears, and bloodshed. He must know the situations she or any of the other Hawks go into…<br /><br />Eew, eeeewww, spit, wipe, rub, just eewww. That is definitely an honor I could do without….ewwwwww….<br /><br />It's a case in which Kaylin learns the truth about the Tha'alani. She also learns Nightshade's lesson about how to retrieve information from others. He does make a good point. She also learns a great deal about the past. What the Tha'alani did, what the Dragons did.<br /><br />Whoa, Sagara keeps letting out these bits and pieces about how lucky Kaylin is to have survived this far. From her first appearance outside the fief with the tattoos, the words, on her arms, she has been an intense topic of discussion with many protectors.<br /><br />And, yet another, whoa, LOL. Sagara is good at this. I keep being surprised that this is only the third installment as I feel I know so much about Kaylin and the others. This particular surprise is Castle Nightshade's rejection of Kaylin. Especially when it's practically sucked her in every other time. A rejection which leads her in an unexpected path to a visual of Tha'alani history and a way to save her own. <br /><br />Andellen has some words of warning regarding her status as <em>Erenne</em>. Whew.<br /><br />Oh, yeah. It's what I love about Kaylin. She just says whatever, wherever, and has no clue that she's being rude. When she does learn it, she is embarrassed, but not enough to take care. It certainly leads to interesting situations.<br /><br /><blockquote>"Don't hate what you can't be<br />Don't hate what you can't have.</blockquote><br /><br />I think this is my favorite of the series so far. Sagara has such great insight and plays it well. It's a story of bigotry and what Kaylin learns. About herself and others. <br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Festival is over. Thank the gods. But criminal action is forever as Kaylin and Severn learn at Evanton's shop.<br /><br />It is in the oldest of the libraries that the action really takes off when Kaylin encounters the skeleton of a not-dead Dragon, for the city is under threat by an element and a renegade mage.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Private <em>Lord</em> Kaylin Neya</strong> is not only a Hawk, but a lord, "a title granted her by the Lord of the Barrani High Court. And, ooh, does that ever tick Kaylin off! It's the metaphysical tattoos on her arms that have catapulted Kaylin into this life of hers. And it's only going to get more interesting.<br /><br /><strong>Corporal Lord Severn Handred</strong> earned his title as well. Only, nobody teases him about it, much to Kaylin's irritation.<br /><br /><strong>Lord Sanabalis</strong> is a Dragon mage who will continue to teach Kaylin how to use her powers. Really, he's all that stands between her and the Emperor. <strong>Lord Tiamaris</strong> is the Dragon who worked with Kaylin and Severn in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9542.Cast_in_Shadow " target="_blank" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Shadow in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Shadow</em>
</a> (1); today, he will return to the Hawks. <strong>Teyaragon</strong> is the oldest of his line, and he accepted a mighty duty to his people. The Imperial Libraries and galleries are <strong>Arkon</strong>'s hoard; the Empire is the <strong>Emperor</strong>'s.<br /><br /><strong>Evanton</strong> is much more than a spells and potion seller. Turns out he's the Keeper of a truly powerful oasis within the city. An elemental garden not governed by the Barrani or the Dragon Emperor.<br /> <br /><em>The Hawks include:</em><br />Iron Jaw, more formally known as Sergeant <strong>Marcus</strong> Kassan, a Leontine Hawk, hands out the assignments and growls at everyone. <strong>Caitlin</strong> is his human assistant and essentially his second-in-command. She only passes Marcus the reports he absolutely must see. They all fear Caitlin's wrath. <strong>Tanner</strong> and <strong>Clint</strong> (of the enticing flight feathers!) are Aerians. <strong>Constant Mallory </strong>is in charge of Missing Persons, and he has a Barrani-like acquaintance with truth.<br /><br /><em>The Tha'alani.</em><br />The <strong>Tha'alani</strong>, a.k.a., Truthseekers, are psychics, mind readers. Their touch is NOT delicate. and their entire society is open about everything---you can't hide what everyone can see anyway. <strong>Ybelline Rabon'alani</strong> is the Emperor's Tha'alani and the leader of her people. She's also the Tha'alani who made Kaylin realize how wrong she was. <strong>Draalzyn</strong> is the Tha'alani at Missing Persons who passes on Ybelline's message. <strong>Epharim</strong> is a guard at the Tha'alani compound. Kaylin's first encounter where she realizes how insular (and why) the Tha'alani are. <strong>Mayalee</strong> is a missing Tha'alani child. <strong>Grethan</strong> is one who was born without the Tha'alani gifts. A handicap so horrible that he fled to the outside world. <strong>Nevaron</strong> and <strong>Onnay</strong> are his friends. <strong>Uriel</strong> was a major figure in Tha'alani history.<br /><br /><strong>Master Sabrai</strong> is in charge of the Oracle Hall. <strong>Everly</strong> is one of the Oracles; his visions are expressed in his paintings. It's the one of Kaylin that is most disturbing.<br /><br /><strong>Lord Nightshade </strong>is an outcaste Barrani fieflord, a crime lord, who has lent his name to his fief where Severn and Kaylin once lived. And he recalls Grethan's time in his fief. <strong>Lord Andellen</strong> was one of the Barrani guards with Kaylin in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30189.Cast_In_Courtlight" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Courtlight in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Courtlight</em>
</a> (2). <br /><br />The <strong>Lord of the Green</strong> is the new castelord, the Lord of the High Halls, with a personal request for Kaylin. His brother, Lirienne, the <strong>Lord of the West March</strong>, still considers Kaylin his <em>kyuthe</em> and likes her very much.<br /><br /><strong>Donalan Idis</strong> was a member of the Arcanum, who worked with the Inquisitorial Services---just one of the reasons why the Tha'alani despise him. The Wolves have been trying to track him down for years.<br /><br />There are three peacekeeping forces and three Lords of Law: the Lord of Hawks, <strong>Lord Grammayre</strong>, the Hawklord, heads up the Hawks---the investigators; the Lord of Swords and his men are the peacekeepers---the street cops, if you will; and, <strong>Lord Merlin</strong>, the Lord of Wolves and his people are its black ops with the Shadow Wolves the "darkest face the Law could turn on the populace".<br /><br />Think of the <strong>Aerians</strong> as birdmen, but not shifters. <strong>Barrani</strong> are the upper class in this society, although not the uppermost. Vicious, cruel, and they seem to have the appearance of what I would consider Fey. The <strong>Leontine</strong> are lion shifters. <strong>Arcanists</strong> are mages who work independently of the Dragon Emperor. <strong>Fieflords</strong> are independent rulers of large neighborhoods outside the city proper.<br /><br /><b>The Cover</b><br />The cover is shades of pink and Indiana Jones with its doubled-in-life-size ancient statues and a leather-clad Kaylin poised to spring into action.<br /><br />The title refers to the history, the evil done that was <em>Cast in Secret</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7961689254857525622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1425467109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1425467109" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30996864-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1425467109?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/30996864-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8632318-cast-in-secret">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1425467109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14408137405758263590"><strong>the ending always brings me to tears</strong><br/><br/>It's a book about resentment, about fear and the suffering it causes...and it's a book about hope and forgiveness and joy, things that mark us even more deeply than the pain, if we let them. Kaylin and Severn's relationship feels more ordinary, here. It's less constrained by horror and bitter hate on Kaylin's side, and by guilt, grief and anger on Severn's. The everyday-ness of their interchanges helps balance their work in unraveling the catastrophe that thre</span>
  <span id="freeText14408137405758263590" style="display:none"><strong>the ending always brings me to tears</strong><br /><br />It's a book about resentment, about fear and the suffering it causes...and it's a book about hope and forgiveness and joy, things that mark us even more deeply than the pain, if we let them. Kaylin and Severn's relationship feels more ordinary, here. It's less constrained by horror and bitter hate on Kaylin's side, and by guilt, grief and anger on Severn's. The everyday-ness of their interchanges helps balance their work in unraveling the catastrophe that threatens their city. Kaylin does a huge amount of growing up in this book, though being Kaylin, she does it with little grace and lots of resentment. She does work her way through her own limitations in the end, and finds her way to grace. Some of the strongest parts of the book for me were Kaylin's encounters with the primal elements. Although their destructive power and grandeur are clearly evident in Sagara's writing, she speaks even more touchingly of their quieter strength in ordinary human life. This book marks a major turning point for Kaylin as she begins to see and understand maturity (at least in other people) and starts to see that her own distorted definition of it offers a disservice to herself and her work. Of course, Kaylin is still Kaylin, and refuses to learn anything too quickly, so don't expect her to change overnight, but by the end of this book she's started to value other people and their experience in ways she has not yet been able to do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14408137405758263590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole Bunge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole Bunge" href="/user/show/1686742-nicole-bunge">Nicole Bunge</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38785044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6197321962653454442">Reviewing this is hard, mainly because I can't tell exactly what it is that I DON'T like about these books, but something nags at me. <br/>Perhaps it's the heroine's(Kaylin Neya) near-inability to mature. She's capable of these insane leaps of instinctual emotional and magical maturity, but behaves like a stubborn 16 yr old the other 80 % of the time. <br/>That being said, the world is well crafted with 4 main races (2 immortal - Dragons and Baranni {oh, just admit they're elves already...} and 2 mortal -</span>
  <span id="freeText6197321962653454442" style="display:none">Reviewing this is hard, mainly because I can't tell exactly what it is that I DON'T like about these books, but something nags at me. <br />Perhaps it's the heroine's(Kaylin Neya) near-inability to mature. She's capable of these insane leaps of instinctual emotional and magical maturity, but behaves like a stubborn 16 yr old the other 80 % of the time. <br />That being said, the world is well crafted with 4 main races (2 immortal - Dragons and Baranni {oh, just admit they're elves already...} and 2 mortal - man and the Tha'alani.) This book focuses on the Tha'alani - who are telepathic humanoids - who have stalks on their heads that can read everyone else's minds through physical contact. <br />I should point out (for personal friends reading this) that this is the 3rd in the series, and the politics of the world are well crafted and (annoyingly) secretive. A lot of questions WON'T be answered, but that's typical given Kaylin's stubborn and shortsighted perspective. Oh well.<br />There's action and magic, lots of emotion - it's thinking man's brain candy. <br />Hardly a proper review, but I'm not amazon.com. I like it, I'll keep reading them. Though I hope the author branches out into other perspectives after this series ends, I'd like to get out of Kaylin's head for a while.</span>

It's likely that books # 1 and # 2 would have driven me bonkers because of her though so starting at the end worked in an odd sort of way. Sagara's writing style kept the story engrossing once I figured out who was who, what they were doing and why. Happy last day of June everyone!</span>

<div id="review_48694910" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48694910" />
    <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship"><img alt="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297107033p2/2109885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48694910?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship">Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=dtb">dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=magic-users">magic-users</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=bye-bye">bye-bye</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=before-goodreads">before-goodreads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48694910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11717138916653237663">Cast in Secret follows on a few days after the second book in the series, Cast in Courtlight. In this instalment a prophetic dream so strong that all of the Oracles even the apprentices receive the same vision, the end of life itself. One very powerful Oracle focuses on Kaylin and begins painting a picture of her on his wall. He is so powerful that he is disabled by his gift. He doesn't speak, he doesn't sleep and he doesn't react like a normal person, his only form of expression is drawing and </span>
  <span id="freeText11717138916653237663" style="display:none">Cast in Secret follows on a few days after the second book in the series, Cast in Courtlight. In this instalment a prophetic dream so strong that all of the Oracles even the apprentices receive the same vision, the end of life itself. One very powerful Oracle focuses on Kaylin and begins painting a picture of her on his wall. He is so powerful that he is disabled by his gift. He doesn't speak, he doesn't sleep and he doesn't react like a normal person, his only form of expression is drawing and painting so Kaylin and co. have to determine who or what could be behind this and how to stop it.<br /><br />Kaylin learns more about the Tha'alani, a telepathic race who can search a person's memory which most find unnerving including Kaylin, and to a lesser extent the Dragons and the Oracles. Kaylin sees Severn in a slightly different light as a Wolf instead of as a Hawk but also how he approaches the Tha'alani - without fear and with a little envy I think. She also learns more about herself, and of the others that have had the marks she has. We are introduced to the elements earth, air, fire and water with the emphasis on water but I won't go into this as I don't want to give anything away. <br /><br />In every book so far (this is the third - the first being Cast in Shadow and the second, Cast in Courtlight) Kaylin has been working through her harrowing past and has been trying to move on. We see her grow not just in her power but as a person and that for me made this an interesting read. <br /><br />There is still plenty of danger surrounding Kaylin especially since it looks like she will be meeting the Dragon Emperor soon. I really enjoyed learning about the Tha'alani, and their history as a people, they are a very interesting race. This series is progressing really well and I'm looking forward to reading the next book, Cast in Fury. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11717138916653237663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_67861750" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67861750" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2169934-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571412324p2/2169934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67861750?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/2169934-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67861750" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8097834637015249740">As my rating of two stars suggests, this book was merely okay, which is a huge letdown after the first two books in the series. However, I'd be lying if I didn't say this was wholly unexpected. The main character, Kaylin Neya, is so introspective, it drives me nuts. She has always tended toward this self indulgent pastime. In this particular novel, it felt as if half the story took place in her thoughts, asides and dysfunctional exchanges with ‘more intelligent’ characters. <br/><br/>I found myself gettin</span>
  <span id="freeText8097834637015249740" style="display:none">As my rating of two stars suggests, this book was merely okay, which is a huge letdown after the first two books in the series. However, I'd be lying if I didn't say this was wholly unexpected. The main character, Kaylin Neya, is so introspective, it drives me nuts. She has always tended toward this self indulgent pastime. In this particular novel, it felt as if half the story took place in her thoughts, asides and dysfunctional exchanges with ‘more intelligent’ characters. <br /><br />I found myself getting more than a little tired of her attitude, her reticence toward just about everything that seems not only a part of her world (magic and politics), but her job! Everyone in the book is so tolerant of her and I found myself starting to dislike her more than a little bit. Not a great way to get through a novel. <br /><br />Finally, where is the romance? All the elements are there, but not indulged. I think a good and proper relationship would improve Kaylin’s outlook immeasurably! I doubt I will rush out for the fourth installment in the series, Cast in Fury. I am not put off enough, however, to try West’s other offerings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8097834637015249740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194640486?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/4193046-amanda">Amanda</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194640486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15429035682021771147">Sometimes I wonder why I've stuck with this series for so long. I've never been particularly excited about it, but something about Kaylin and Elantra intrigues me. Plus, I've been reading so much urban fantasy/paranormal novels lately that something a little more high fantasy is welcome.<br/><br/>Cast in Secret picks up not long after the ending of Cast in Courtlight, and, just like in previous installments, Kaylin, the Hawk from Nightshade with the mysterious magical markings, must track down a missing g</span>
  <span id="freeText15429035682021771147" style="display:none">Sometimes I wonder why I've stuck with this series for so long. I've never been particularly excited about it, but something about Kaylin and Elantra intrigues me. Plus, I've been reading so much urban fantasy/paranormal novels lately that something a little more high fantasy is welcome.<br /><br />Cast in Secret picks up not long after the ending of Cast in Courtlight, and, just like in previous installments, Kaylin, the Hawk from Nightshade with the mysterious magical markings, must track down a missing girl. Meanwhile the city's Oracles predict that Elantra will be destroyed in two weeks. Kind of interesting, but tends to feel just a little cliche and somewhat like a retread of previous books.<br /><br />While the writing has improved in Cast in Secret, the characters continue to feel incredibly stagnant, particularly Kaylin. While I understand that there are still more books in the series to come, there hasn't been any change or maturity in her character, which makes her feel unrealistic and hard to like.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book for what it was and will probably continue the series just to see what happens next, but I wouldn't recommend it to readers who didn't enjoy the previous books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15429035682021771147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer994037912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12016688667870826281">By this point in the series I was seriously hoping to see a change for the better in the writing. Hello, editor, where were you on this one? I did not enjoy being told the same information over and over, and over again. Especially while other parts of the story that could have been of interest were underdeveloped. Another beef I had with this one was that there was a whole lot of talking and thinking but you couldn't always be sure who it was coming from and their message was often not clearly c</span>
  <span id="freeText12016688667870826281" style="display:none">By this point in the series I was seriously hoping to see a change for the better in the writing. Hello, editor, where were you on this one? I did not enjoy being told the same information over and over, and over again. Especially while other parts of the story that could have been of interest were underdeveloped. Another beef I had with this one was that there was a whole lot of talking and thinking but you couldn't always be sure who it was coming from and their message was often not clearly conveyed. Also, the author failed to adequately describe and put her characters into motion. What does Severn look like? Can't tell ya. But I know he's got dark eyes, a scar and some hair that sometimes hangs in his face. He doesn't move much either, or that is to say, there is no detail about how he moves. He just gets there. Most of the characters seem to have this problem on one or more occasion. When they should move they just stand or just sit. I was most annoyed by this in the case of Nightshade and Kaylin where in more than one scene their positioning was wrong for the movements described or there was a complete lack of descriptive movement for far to long. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12016688667870826281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5466569479717950616">This is a really strong installment of the Elantra books. I enjoyed the plot of this one much more than the 2nd book but didn't *really* enjoy it until the final climax, which I could barely read, it was so exciting. <br/><br/>And ok, after this book, I think </span>
  <span id="freeText5466569479717950616" style="display:none">This is a really strong installment of the Elantra books. It starts as a crime investigation of 2 seemingly unconnected missing persons cases and then dives into the elemental magic system, the nature of the oracles, and the world of the Tha'alani, a telepathic race that socially functions as a collective. I enjoyed the plot of this one much more than the 2nd book but didn't *really* enjoy it until the final climax, which I could barely read, it was so exciting. <br /><br />And ok, after this book, I think I get the whole Nightshade thing, but I'm still all about Severn. Yes, he's overprotective and too guarded at times, but their history together is just so compelling. But I've read reviews of all 6 books that are out at this point, and I *cannot* believe nothing has happened with either of them yet!! What's up with that?</span>

In the moments where she is being magically tested, she exhibits a wisdom and intuitive sense that is encouraging. However in her everyday demeanor, she continues to be difficult.   <span id="freeText16201604713824021589" style="display:none">I am still enjoying this series...the only thing that keeps this from being a 5-star is I'm not seeing much evidence that Kaylin is learning/growing from all of her experiences. In the moments where she is being magically tested, she exhibits a wisdom and intuitive sense that is encouraging. However in her everyday demeanor, she continues to be difficult. There's only so much foot-stomping petulance, naive bumbling, and willful ignorance that I can take before it gets tiresome. Although it was nice to see Kaylin conquer one of her prejudices in this story. There is a wonderful cast of characters surrounding Kaylin, and I really hope that she grows up soon. I continue to be fascinated with the world of Elantra, the magical places of the Old Ones, and getting more of a glimpse into the history of the Tha'alani and Dragon races.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12881730771696982283">Maybe it says something that I find these books easier to engage with now I've turned up the audio narration speed? Anyway, I liked this better than the second book. Interesting enough storyline and a strong theme with regard to belonging, and how even accidental outcasts can turn vicious. We still see very little of Kaylin's interpersonal relationships. I'm not looking for romance but she has to be more than just her job. Worldbuilding fantastic as usual; prose style bogged down with repetition</span>
  <span id="freeText12881730771696982283" style="display:none">Maybe it says something that I find these books easier to engage with now I've turned up the audio narration speed? Anyway, I liked this better than the second book. Interesting enough storyline and a strong theme with regard to belonging, and how even accidental outcasts can turn vicious. We still see very little of Kaylin's interpersonal relationships. I'm not looking for romance but she has to be more than just her job. Worldbuilding fantastic as usual; prose style bogged down with repetition and expositionary dialogue also as usual. I liked this enough to keep going with the series. </span>

<div id="review_62901097" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62901097" />
    <a title="Heather Faye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1232484-heather-faye"><img alt="Heather Faye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471746648p2/1232484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62901097?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather Faye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather Faye" href="/user/show/1232484-heather-faye">Heather Faye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1232484-heather-faye?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62901097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1338000982334154651">This will be the written review for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9542.Cast_in_Shadow__Chronicles_of_Elantra__Book_1_' title='Cast in Shadow (Chronicles of Elantra, Book 1) by Michelle Sagara West' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cast in Shadow Chronicles of Elantra Book 1</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6256.Michelle_Sagara_West' title='Michelle Sagara West' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michelle Sagara West</a> and it's series partners, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30189.Cast_In_Courtlight__Chronicles_of_Elantra__Book_2_' title='Cast In Courtlight (Chronicles of Elantra, Book 2) by Michelle Sagara West' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cast in Courtlight Chronicles of Elantra Book 2</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3284487.Cast_In_Secret__Chronicles_of_Elantra__Book_3_' title='Cast In Secret (Chronicles of Elantra, Book 3) by Michelle Sagara West' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cast in Secret Chronicles of Elantra Book 3</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Cast%20in%20Shadow%20Chronicles%20of%20Fury%20Book%204' title='Cast in Shadow Chronicles of Fury Book 4' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cast in Shadow Chronicles of Fury Book 4</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304351.Cast_in_Silence__Chronicles_of_Elantra__Book_5_' title='Cast in Silence (Chronicles of Elantra, Book 5) by Michelle Sagara West' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cast in Silence Chronicles of Elantra Book 5</a>.<br/><br/>I read this series three times. It was engaging but had a few annoying issues. The world of Elantra was well created and very detailed. I admired the multiple species and the troublesom</span>
  <span id="freeText1338000982334154651" style="display:none">This will be the written review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9542.Cast_in_Shadow__Chronicles_of_Elantra__Book_1_" title="Cast in Shadow (Chronicles of Elantra, Book 1) by Michelle Sagara West" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Shadow Chronicles of Elantra Book 1</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6256.Michelle_Sagara_West" title="Michelle Sagara West" rel="nofollow noopener">Michelle Sagara West</a> and it's series partners, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30189.Cast_In_Courtlight__Chronicles_of_Elantra__Book_2_" title="Cast In Courtlight (Chronicles of Elantra, Book 2) by Michelle Sagara West" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Courtlight Chronicles of Elantra Book 2</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3284487.Cast_In_Secret__Chronicles_of_Elantra__Book_3_" title="Cast In Secret (Chronicles of Elantra, Book 3) by Michelle Sagara West" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Secret Chronicles of Elantra Book 3</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Cast%20in%20Shadow%20Chronicles%20of%20Fury%20Book%204" title="Cast in Shadow Chronicles of Fury Book 4" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Shadow Chronicles of Fury Book 4</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304351.Cast_in_Silence__Chronicles_of_Elantra__Book_5_" title="Cast in Silence (Chronicles of Elantra, Book 5) by Michelle Sagara West" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Silence Chronicles of Elantra Book 5</a>.<br /><br />I read this series three times. It was engaging but had a few annoying issues. The world of Elantra was well created and very detailed. I admired the multiple species and the troublesome interactions they had to encounter. I thought the author had a wonderful idea for a series of books and I very much enjoyed the stories. <br /><br />However, these books, in my opinion, were not edited nearly hard enough. Sentences ran along for paragraphs at a time. The use of the hyphen was used annoyingly often and sometimes incorrectly. I do not lay these errors at the authors feet. These are things that should have been fixed in the editing process and were not. An author becomes close to their work. Perhaps with some tough editing these could have been great books. Instead, they were average books and not ones I would recommend to the average fantasy reader. I read them because I knew I had things to gain in world development from them. <br /><br />The other highly bothersome issue was in naming. There were numerous character's named similarly and it caused some confusion in the reading. This is really a pet peeve and not something I would judge a book on solely. However, with other issues, it just creates a more confusing read. All in all, if you are a die hard fantasy fan or plan to write in the genre, these are worth a gander, otherwise, not so much. Each book is stared for it's individual story enjoyment. Without the editing problems, they would have scored much higher in my opinion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1338000982334154651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B9a/MiznAz5XqmT3C9T5Qdp1cL5A7EJ+CuHwj/8Q+Rl2NCI4IBJUcrNcWWLMrykoc10kiiEbu1L99BjC+DEt/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
